                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2018/01/robotics-project-pltw-pull-toy.html">
                      Robotics Project! PLTW Pull Toy
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-9189810509737019200">
                     Hey there! Does anyone teach PLTW Gateway Automation &amp; Robotics? I do. We do a project called Pull Toy and I made an animoto to help me introduce the project. You can use it if you want!
                     <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="360" id="vp1pHnXV" src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/embed.animoto.com/play.html?w=swf/production/vp1&amp;e=1516807111&amp;f=pHnXVG1cInH4EKEuVYBYRA&amp;d=0&amp;m=a&amp;r=360p+480p+720p&amp;volume=100&amp;start_res=0p&amp;i=m&amp;asset_domain=s3-p.animoto.com&amp;animoto_domain=animoto.com&amp;options=autostart" title="Video Player" width="640">
                     </iframe>

                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, October 31, 2017
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="3041058539130998993">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2017/10/a-little-star-wars-3d-printing-on-my.html">
                      A Little Star Wars 3D Printing On My Work Break Today--Happy Halloween!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3041058539130998993">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-eeLCSUwWk28/WfioKFHrfuI/AAAAAAAAjgg/3MVsuMr-FgkUFmXM6NOXO2RwZR826aemQCLcBGAs/s1600/17317705.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" data-original-height="520" data-original-width="520" height="320" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-eeLCSUwWk28/WfioKFHrfuI/AAAAAAAAjgg/3MVsuMr-FgkUFmXM6NOXO2RwZR826aemQCLcBGAs/s320/17317705.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     I am dressed as Obi Wan, today. May the force be with you.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I love my costume, but there is no way for me to clip the lightsaber to my belt. Until now. The photo to the right shows the lightsaber I bought at Target. The clip I designed and printed today holds it onto my belt. It snaps onto the handle of the saber.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     This lightsaber clip that I designed on Autodesk Inventor was printed on an Ultimaker 2+, with a 4mm nozzle, using PLA at normal resolution. Infill at 50%.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Please take a look and download the files here:
                     <br/>
                     <a href="https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:2617609">
                      https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:2617609
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-oAGjarU--aY/WfiuWiB3DlI/AAAAAAAAjgw/oBiphXsXCQoxqviV9-0F_P9xEP6zq9crgCLcBGAs/s1600/lightsaber%2Bholster.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" data-original-height="702" data-original-width="891" height="252" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-oAGjarU--aY/WfiuWiB3DlI/AAAAAAAAjgw/oBiphXsXCQoxqviV9-0F_P9xEP6zq9crgCLcBGAs/s320/lightsaber%2Bholster.png" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, November 16, 2016
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="6525278967405641633">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/11/pltw-automation-robotics-kahoot.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: PLTW Automation &amp; Robotics Kahoot!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6525278967405641633">
                     This Kahoot! is a fun way to review and learn the names of VEX Robotics parts and gear ratios.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="" data-bypass="" href="https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/82b9198e-5b1e-4e61-b0ad-fa69efaf37c7" style='background-color: white; color: #41c4dd; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; outline: 0px;' target="_blank">
                      https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/82b9198e-5b1e-4e61-b0ad-fa69efaf37c7
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ijqqS1k5knk/WCyI2pg6bUI/AAAAAAAAewU/Uq15vmUCwnITW9BElYpeib5Gf4OkHXRMACLcB/s1600/vex%2Bparts%2Bkahoot.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="147" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ijqqS1k5knk/WCyI2pg6bUI/AAAAAAAAewU/Uq15vmUCwnITW9BElYpeib5Gf4OkHXRMACLcB/s400/vex%2Bparts%2Bkahoot.png" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Teaching Tools Series: PLTW Automation &amp; Robotics Kahoot!
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">

                    <a name="6693946907973333516">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/11/caliper-practice-block.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Caliper Practice Block
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6693946907973333516">
                     So, I teach
                     <a href="https://www.pltw.org/our-programs/pltw-gateway" target="_blank">
                      PLTW Gateway
                     </a>
                     courses (
                     <a href="https://www.pltw.org/our-programs/pltw-gateway" target="_blank">
                      Design &amp; Modeling
                     </a>
                     and
                     <a href="https://www.pltw.org/our-programs/pltw-gateway-curriculum#curriculum-2" target="_blank">
                      Automation &amp; Robotics
                     </a>
                     ). In Design &amp; Modeling (DM), I teach students to use calipers as a precise and accurate measuring tool.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <span style="text-align: center;">
                       See my assessment ideas, and download all of the files for free at:
                      </span>
                      <a href="http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:1878943" style="text-align: center;">
                       http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:1878943
                      </a>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I have 2cm interlocking blocks that come with the curriculum materials for PLTW, but I wanted something with larger and more varied dimensions for the students to measure. I also wanted the object to cause students to use the different tools that are on the caliper.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     So, I created this:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-vRT7Qx2qyYk/WCxXiqn6VLI/AAAAAAAAevE/V9juRTagGtYWrYxKJS7DHiYlUop4XOAEgCLcB/s1600/Screenshot%2B%252815%2529.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="257" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-vRT7Qx2qyYk/WCxXiqn6VLI/AAAAAAAAevE/V9juRTagGtYWrYxKJS7DHiYlUop4XOAEgCLcB/s400/Screenshot%2B%252815%2529.png" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         See my assessment ideas, and download all of the files for free at:
                         <a href="http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:1878943">
                          http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:1878943
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     I printed several of them out on an Ultimaker 2 and I use them to assess my students' caliper skills or give them extra practice.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-3hHdj12WasA/WCxYmAm7F0I/AAAAAAAAevQ/wySou1pp0lsGT_ugTkvFLBx-Nefdu0NsACLcB/s1600/caliper%2Bblock.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="300" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-3hHdj12WasA/WCxYmAm7F0I/AAAAAAAAevQ/wySou1pp0lsGT_ugTkvFLBx-Nefdu0NsACLcB/s400/caliper%2Bblock.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Caliper Practice Block
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/11/caliper-practice-block.html";
                     </script>
                     <script src="http://static.addtoany.com/menu/page.js" type="text/javascript">
                     </script>

                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, March 2, 2016
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="1402870203771053458">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/03/makerbotlearning-loves-my-swiss-cheese.html">
                      MakerBotLearning Loves My Swiss Cheese Chair!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1402870203771053458">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-6aIzeo0mVNQ/Vtbn3ko9vQI/AAAAAAAAb1s/wYm1tipng9E/s1600/photo_preview_featured.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-6aIzeo0mVNQ/Vtbn3ko9vQI/AAAAAAAAb1s/wYm1tipng9E/s320/photo_preview_featured.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/df/64/fa/36/3d/Swiss_Cheese_Chair_preview_featured.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="http://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/df/64/fa/36/3d/Swiss_Cheese_Chair_preview_featured.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     This
                     <a href="http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:414725" target="_blank">
                      Swiss Cheese Chair
                     </a>
                     <a href="http://www.thingiverse.com/make:102711" target="_blank">
                     </a>
                     is the
                     <strike>
                      first
                     </strike>
                     <i>
                      only
                     </i>
                     3D print file that I ever designed myself from scratch. Apparently,
                     <a href="http://www.thingiverse.com/make:102711" target="_blank">
                      the folks at MakerBot headquarters in Brooklyn, NYC loved it
                     </a>
                     ! I texted Drew at MakerBot after this was posted, and he said since the print comes out so well and is a fast print, tons of people in the office printed them in different sizes and placed them around the office on their desks!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Super fun. The Swiss Cheese Chair Universe is arriving. Slowly. Print by print. It's a movement! Maybe I'll print one and send it to Bernie Sanders.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I don't have a MakerBot anymore, I have a couple of Ultimaker 2+ printers. I'll post the print from the Ultimakers later...I only have silver filament for now, though.
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      MakerBotLearning Loves My Swiss Cheese Chair!
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/03/makerbotlearning-loves-my-swiss-cheese.html";
                     </script>

                     </script>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, March 1, 2016
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="2026276409057125580">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/03/reason-149-why-i-love-my-job.html">
                      Reason #149 Why I Love My Job:
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2026276409057125580">
                     <div>
                      Scene:
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      While the hallway still teems with kids moving from class to class, the door to the classroom quietly opens and shuts, noise filtering in bursts.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      The first three students arrive, to a quiet and ready classroom--the work reminders for the day bright on the interactive wall of the lab.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      "Good morning, Mrs. Kaplan. Should we wait for you or can we just get started building?"
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      Students say those words to me.
                      <i>
                       Before
                      </i>
                      the bell. Every. Single. Day.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      It is music to my ears.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ynztZGAv13w/VtYewq_KtZI/AAAAAAAAb08/0_xj6BQF4_k/s1600/Robotics.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="225" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ynztZGAv13w/VtYewq_KtZI/AAAAAAAAb08/0_xj6BQF4_k/s400/Robotics.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Everyone's doing something different in my classroom, but they're all working on the same project.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <br/>

                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Reason #149 Why I Love My Job:
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/03/reason-149-why-i-love-my-job.html";
                     </script>

                     </script>

                    </div>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Thursday, February 25, 2016
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="6703375885606993613">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/02/teaching-tools-series-kahoot-in-stem.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Kahoot! in the STEM classroom--FREE
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6703375885606993613">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-4IB3JrB-AaA/Vs-JiXuGHuI/AAAAAAAAby8/Pn5H8tkCiAI/s1600/tumblr_inline_n5za5h2ToY1rgp1yg.gif" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="213" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-4IB3JrB-AaA/Vs-JiXuGHuI/AAAAAAAAby8/Pn5H8tkCiAI/s320/tumblr_inline_n5za5h2ToY1rgp1yg.gif" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     Wow. That gif is...gify.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Now that I have your attention, if you haven't used
                     <a href="http://getkahoot.com/" target="_blank">
                      Kahoot!
                     </a>
                     in your classroom yet, you're in for a real treat. Kahoot! is full of user-created ready-made interactive quiz games that make Jeopardy buzzer systems completely and utterly irrelevant. Sorry, Alex Trebec. Here's the Kahoot! game that I used in my class today--try it out for FREE on the Kahoot! community board:
                     <br/>
                     <a href="https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/38ec8f09-d42a-497f-b4f9-68b009bbd586">
                      https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/38ec8f09-d42a-497f-b4f9-68b009bbd586
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     If you like it, you can join Kahoot! (also free) and start playing right away. For how much? You guessed it: it's free. Student accounts--also free.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://community.kahoot.it/uploads/default/148/a03ff06569e8fb08.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="239" src="https://community.kahoot.it/uploads/default/148/a03ff06569e8fb08.png" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     Students can use whichever device they have handy--but in my experience, the kids favor touchscreens because of the reaction-time advantage. You don't even need a projector, really, depending on your class size. I have used my HD laptop in a pinch. Today, this is what my 8th grade class looked like playing Kahoot!--we were waiting for a guest speaker to arrive and it was an engaging and fun activity as well as a good way to review material.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yzuysUdCod0/Vs-RBXRcPZI/AAAAAAAAbzM/J5oElP438fI/s1600/kahoot.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="225" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-yzuysUdCod0/Vs-RBXRcPZI/AAAAAAAAbzM/J5oElP438fI/s400/kahoot.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         This is TWO class sections of eighth graders happy and busy
                         <br/>
                         while they wait for our guest speaker to arrive! Yes! It really happens!
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     How it works: you choose a Kahoot! quiz to use and then Launch it to your device/projector. The students login using the URL and the login code to access your quiz in real time. They add their username (they do NOT need accounts--this is the best part). Once everyone joins the quiz, the quiz will launch!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Some fun music plays in the background while a question pops up on the big screen and on their devices. They have to wait a few moments until the multiple-choice answers pop up on the screen, and then they get access to punch in their response on their device.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     One of the coolest parts of this is that it's really interactive in the whole-class sense. They aren't staring at the board or their device. They all have to constantly look up at the board and then down at their devices and then back at the board to see if they were right. The leaderboard is posted after every question--extra points for speed! It's not unusual for students to jump out of their seats with excitement as they see where they are in the lineup.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-LJgO_nueUic/Vs-S_sAVrPI/AAAAAAAAbzY/o0I9aONS-3k/s1600/learnersto%2Bleaders.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="222" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-LJgO_nueUic/Vs-S_sAVrPI/AAAAAAAAbzY/o0I9aONS-3k/s400/learnersto%2Bleaders.png" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Kahoot! Markets itself as tool that can be flipped to let the kids create.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     I teach a couple of PLTW courses and this Kahoot! is specifically for Automation and Robotics, Lesson 2.2.2 Mechanisms. Give it a try alone or with a few friends to see what Kahoot! is all about.
                     <a href="https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/38ec8f09-d42a-497f-b4f9-68b009bbd586">
                      https://play.kahoot.it/#/k/38ec8f09-d42a-497f-b4f9-68b009bbd586
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     You can create your own Kahoot!, customizing it for your particular classroom and lesson. You can easily embed photos and youtube videos that enhance your quizzes. What's fantastic, though, is there are thousands of user-created quizzes that are just waiting for your tweaks to make them perfect or you can use them as-is.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     **FYI, I am not a paid spokesperson for Kahoot! nor do they sponsor me in any way. I just really like this tool.
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Kahoot! in the STEM classroom--FREE
                     </p>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, February 23, 2016
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="4065143919320402949">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/02/stem-studio-coding-story-assignment-on.html">
                      STEM Studio: Coding a Story Assignment on Scratch--Free Lesson Plan and Worksheet!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4065143919320402949">
                     In a peculiar plot twist, for the last few years I've been a full-time STEM teacher. I teach engineering, robotics, computer programming and 3D modeling to middle schoolers. Best. Job. Ever.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     In my 6th grade class, the students are learning computer programming using Scratch. I have a student that is quite a gifted animator. One assignment focused on creating a story, complete with a plot, theme, characters, conflict and resolution. She created a character for the story called Cake Troll.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I am obsessed with Cake Troll. I want to hug Cake Troll. I want to wipe his tears, he's so adorable. Here is the story:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a href="https://www.blogger.com/goog_719084506">
                      <iframe allowfullscreen="" allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" height="402" src="//scratch.mit.edu/projects/embed/93197078/?autostart=false" width="485">
                      </iframe>
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <a href="https://scratch.mit.edu/projects/93197078/">
                      https://scratch.mit.edu/projects/93197078/
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     This young lady is in 6th grade! Yeah, I know. She's a really gifted animator. Anyway, I wanted to share my project plans with you in case you'd like to do the same lesson with your students.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <i>
                       <u>
                        Resources:
                       </u>
                      </i>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <ul>
                      <li>
                       Digital copy of Story Map
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Video of
                       <u>
                        <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=j5lL8biSz6E" target="_blank">
                         Tick Tock Tale
                        </a>
                       </u>
                       or other animated short story
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       printed copies of Story Map for each student
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       SCRATCH account for each student at
                       <a href="http://mit.scratch.edu/">
                        mit.scratch.edu
                       </a>
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       3-5 class periods of 45 minutes each
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      1. Engage interest in the lesson by showing a good short story. I like to use Disney's
                      <u>
                       Tick Tock Tale
                      </u>
                      because there's no dialogue to distract from the little clocks that are bursting with personality. It also enables kids to think more critically about story elements, because they are open to interpretation without dialogue. It's interesting how certain students will focus on the little clock feeling lonely, or left out and some won't pick up on that at all! Here's a clip:
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <iframe allowfullscreen="" class="YOUTUBE-iframe-video" data-thumbnail-src="https://i.ytimg.com/vi/j5lL8biSz6E/0.jpg" frameborder="0" height="266" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/j5lL8biSz6E?feature=player_embedded" width="320">
                      </iframe>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     2. Project
                     <a href="https://docs.google.com/document/d/1pSy_0TluYY6kO5zVTzG5c6RRxz8oeALuCXynWCbZQY4/edit?usp=sharing" target="_blank">
                      this Story Map
                     </a>
                     . Discuss each story element to remind kids of what they are (this is a STEM class, so I really depend on the Language Arts department for doing some seriously good teaching on story structure).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     3. Watch the video again, if you have time, and fill in the map as you go (or afterward).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     4. Explain that they will be programming stories in Scratch, but they need to plan out their story before they begin. One way to develop a good project is to plan it out. In Scratch,
                     <a href="http://scratch.mit.edu/projects/91099302/" target="_blank">
                      create a Studio
                     </a>
                     full of projects that you think are good examples of short stories. You could also use this studio if you like, which is filled with projects that my own students created or projects that I just thought were cool--for better or for worse! Many of these kids are 11 or 12 years old, don't be too critical. Lots of them have never coded before.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     5. Work in groups to brainstorm ideas and create a story map. Each student should make their own, or you can let them work in groups on the project. After they get you to check their work they can start coding on Scratch!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     6. After they are done, gather all the projects in another Studio. I do this step by posting an assignment on Google Classroom and having them submit the
                     <i>
                      shared
                     </i>
                     link to their project as an ADD&gt;LINK.
                     <br/>
                     Share the link to the studio with your students (I use Google Classroom for this also).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <u>
                       Good Digital Citizenship (GDC)
                      </u>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     7. In another class period, we share our projects and practice commenting using
                     <i style="font-weight: bold;">
                      specific, constructive and supportive feedback.
                     </i>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      STEM Studio: Coding a Story Assignment on Scratch--Free Lesson Plan and Worksheet!
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2016/02/stem-studio-coding-story-assignment-on.html";
                     </script>
                     <script src="http://static.addtoany.com/menu/page.js" type="text/javascript">
                     </script>
                     <div style="clear: both;">
                     </div>
                    </div>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, April 1, 2015
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="4619305125126758102">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2015/04/were-taking-sbac.html">
                      We're Taking SBAC!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4619305125126758102">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      Two amazing teachers at my school, Alison Jasgur and Sarah O'Mahoney, created this video for all teachers, administrators and staff in the US who are now administering the SBAC. SBAC tests are the new computer based tests published by the
                      <a href="http://www.smarterbalanced.org/" target="_blank">
                       Smarter Balanced Assessments Consortium
                      </a>
                      in conjunction with the changes to Language Arts and Mathematics standards in the
                      <a href="http://www.corestandards.org/" target="_blank">
                       Common Core.
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <iframe allowfullscreen="" class="YOUTUBE-iframe-video" data-thumbnail-src="https://i.ytimg.com/vi/zxFbdKnIQcc/0.jpg" frameborder="0" height="266" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/zxFbdKnIQcc?feature=player_embedded" width="320">
                      </iframe>
                     </div>

                     </a>

                      We're Taking SBAC!
                     </p>

                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Thursday, February 26, 2015
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="4359754839032934259">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2015/02/ted-ed-featured-lesson-on-science-in.html">
                      TED Ed Featured Lesson on Science in the Renaissance: Galileo Discover's Moons of Jupiter
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4359754839032934259">
                     Hey there readers!
                     <br/>
                     Want a fun lesson to share with your friends, family, children or pets?
                     <br/>
                     TED Ed challenged me (yes, I was there with them at the TED Ed HQ in New York...was AWESOME!) to produce a "lesson flip" on the Renaissance.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I'm a science teacher, so my lesson was about Galileo.
                     <a href="http://ed.ted.com/on/NGTNgZiC#watch">
                      http://ed.ted.com/on/NGTNgZiC#watch
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Each TED Ed flipped lesson has a video component, an online "quiz", additional links or online activities, a discussion question and some food for thought in the form of a famous quote on the topic.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     This lesson was featured on the TED Ed blog:
                     <br/>
                     <a href="http://blog.ed.ted.com/2013/09/16/top-five-videos-to-flip-the-renaissance/">
                      http://blog.ed.ted.com/2013/09/16/top-five-videos-to-flip-the-renaissance/
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      TED Ed Featured Lesson on Science in the Renaissance: Galileo Discover's Moons of Jupiter

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Saturday, February 7, 2015
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="2194058621142078144">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2015/02/stemsteam-games-that-rock-part-2.html">
                      STEM/STEAM Games that Rock! Part 2
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2194058621142078144">
                     Today's app definitely has an artistic side.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Art materials feature largely in our home. My kids have watercolor easels, their own sketchbooks, pencil boxes and they are very particular about
                     <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Staedtler-2-Hole-Metal-Pencil-Sharpener/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
                      their pencil sharpeners
                     </a>
                     . You have to know your pencil sharpeners to have a favorite.  My husband is an artist and we have his, and his friends' large canvases, his grandparents' oil paintings, and his mothers' watercolors all around our home. We have a painting studio in our house. STEM has turned to STEAM around here. I also prefer to have the kids actually
                     <i>
                      making
                     </i>
                     something when they have screen time. Many people will happily listen to kids talk about art or comic strips that they made, but no one (I've done a survey) wants to listen to kids talk about levels they completed on Skylanders.
                     <br/>
                     <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: left; margin-right: 1em; text-align: left;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-S-MW--oBGn0/VNawS5UWfBI/AAAAAAAAV6g/E4Foc1JNzP0/s1600/Strip%2BDesigner%2B-%2BEdited.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-S-MW--oBGn0/VNawS5UWfBI/AAAAAAAAV6g/E4Foc1JNzP0/s1600/Strip%2BDesigner%2B-%2BEdited.jpg" width="285"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         A comic my son created by using photos and tools.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <u>
                       Strip Designer
                      </u>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     In our house, we are comic-book fanatics. My husband has been collecting comic books since he was a little kid. He grew up in Brooklyn in the 70s, when his parents would give him 35 cents to go to the corner store to buy a comic book with change left over for penny candy. Now we have an entire storage room in our basement dedicated to vintage and new comic books. We watch all the hero movies while my husband whispers each character's backstory into our ears as the film rolls on.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a href="http://www.mexircus.com/Strip_Designer/" target="_blank">
                      Strip Designer
                     </a>
                     and our kids are a match made in heaven. They have many different templates, styles and tools that you can use to overlay on your own photography. The strip shown here that my son made took him about an hour or so with my help as photographer, but we were learning how the tools worked. Tools are robust, and would appeal to experienced artists as well as kids. There are advanced editing tools like layers and other fancy things that I don't know how to use.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      STEM/STEAM Games that Rock! Part 2
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2015/02/stemsteam-games-that-rock-part-2.html";
                     </script>
                     <script src="http://static.addtoany.com/menu/page.js" type="text/javascript">
                     </script>

                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2015/02/stem-games-that-rock.html">
                      STEM/STEAM games that Rock! Part 1
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7714980340285208906">
                     As a mom, blogger and Science Technology Engineering (Arts) and Math teacher, I'm always checking out new math, science, puzzle or invention apps and trying them out on my children. Here's a list of the ones I or one of my children has obsessed over in the last month. I usually get my recommendations from Graphite, because I have a full time job at work, at home
                     <i>
                      and
                     </i>
                     I'm a coach (not for sports, for STEM, but more on that another day).
                     <br/>
                     <a href="http://ipadstory.ru/wp-content/uploads/2011/02/IMG_0281.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                      <img border="0" height="240" src="http://ipadstory.ru/wp-content/uploads/2011/02/IMG_0281.jpg" width="320"/>
                     </a>
                     <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/tinkerbox-hd/id415722219?mt=8" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
                      <b style="text-decoration: underline;">
                       Tinkerbox
                      </b>
                     </a>
                     This jewel of an engineering app was brought into the world by Autodesk of AutoCAD fame. These folks over there are SERIOUS engineers and yet, my seven year old can play this game for quite a while. I love to watch him play. He loves the music and says he finds it calming and that it "helps him solve the problems".
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.wired.com/wp-content/uploads/blogs/geekdad/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/DragonBox-step1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="240" src="http://www.wired.com/wp-content/uploads/blogs/geekdad/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/DragonBox-step1.jpg" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Dragon Box after playing for 5 minutes
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     What I particularly love about this iPad app is that he is constantly in the "Develop and Prototype/Test the Solution" loop of the
                     <a href="https://www.teachengineering.org/engrdesignprocess.php">
                      Engineering Design Process.
                     </a>
                     This little guy adjusts the position of the catapult button or electric fan by a millimeter, tests it and then readjusts as many times as necessary until he achieves SUCCESS!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <u>
                       DragonBox 5+ and DragonBox 12+
                      </u>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     Dude, the kids ask me to do Algebra. Every. Day. My 7 year old solved a multivariable equation for x (the dragonbox) after playing this game for 45 minutes. Zoinks! There are two versions, 5+ and 12+, according to age. Definitely play this game with your kid. It's math like it shoulda been! The sound effects and graphics remind me a little of World of Goo meets OmNom from Cut the Rope (both excellent STEM apps, also!) and the sound effect when you isolate the DragonBox is like a light saber!
                     <a href="http://archive.wired.com/geekdad/2012/06/dragonbox/all/" target="_blank">
                      GeekDad at Wired Magazine
                     </a>
                     went crazy over how it was better than angry birds.
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://cs3-4.4pda.to/3684925.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="200" src="http://cs3-4.4pda.to/3684925.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     That's all I have time for right now, gotta put the kids to bed and get ready to teach my Engineering &amp; Design classes tomorrow! More tomorrow...
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      STEM/STEAM games that Rock! Part 1
                     </p>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Saturday, May 25, 2013
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="8913767740246430679">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/05/ted-publishes-my-video-on-ted-ed.html">
                      TED Publishes My Video on TED-Ed!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8913767740246430679">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="266" mozallowfullscreen="mozallowfullscreen" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/DD_8Jm5pTLk?feature=player_embedded" webkitallowfullscreen="webkitallowfullscreen" width="320">
                      </iframe>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I haven't had a chance to post about the video production process much, but here is basically how it went down:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <ol>
                      <a href="http://www.atscomms.com/FUZZY1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em; text-align: center;">
                       <img border="0" height="200" src="http://www.atscomms.com/FUZZY1.jpg" width="165"/>
                      </a>
                      <li>
                       A friend nominated me on the
                       <a href="http://ed.ted.com/lessons/reasons-for-the-seasons-rebecca-kaplan">
                        TED-Ed website.
                       </a>
                       You can nominate your friends, too (or yourself!) by clicking the
                       <a href="http://ed.ted.com/get_involved">
                        "Get Involved"
                       </a>
                       link.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Jordan Reeves, head of TED Ed, sent me an email to set up a time to talk on the phone about possibilities. At this point, they make it pretty clear that the whole thing is completely exploratory--no guarantees.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       I agreed to try to write a script for a three minute video.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Discovered that writing a script for a good three minute video is really, really challenging.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Sent the script to the editorial team. Bit my nails for several weeks.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       The editorial team decided that they liked the script! Hooray! I made it to round three. This one's easy--all I have to do is take a look at their suggested edits and check for scientific accuracy.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       I have decided that all writers should have professional editors: I am not a writer, but their editing added a certain
                       <i>
                        je ne sais quoi
                       </i>
                       to the wording in my script. Definitely better than it was when I sent it.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Round Four: record the voiceover. Since I live close to New York City, and I was on vacation at the time, I made the trip down to the TED Ed offices in Chelsea to use their cute little recording booth. Rose, the science journalist and voiceover editor, directed me through the recording. I did not have to go down to the office--if you live far away, they send you a 'portable recording studio'.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Then, I have to wait. And bite nails more. They send the voiceover and script out to a group of selected professional animators and wait until an animator chooses a voiceover. If you don't get chosen, that's the end of that. The reason the animators have the choice is because they often put in many MANY hours to put the videos together--and these are real professional who are volunteering their work hours (kind of like the teachers that put the lessons together). Some of these guys/gals work for places like Pixar and Dreamworks. Others just rock on their own.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Marc Christoforidis picks my script! WOW! I am so excited.
                       <a href="https://vimeo.com/58839267">
                        Here is his professional reel on Vimeo.
                       </a>
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Then, we work together...emailing back and forth for weeks. He sends me animated sketches (animatics) and stills to get my feedback and so I can check for accuracy. He did an amazing job of interpreting some difficult places in the script. I never even saw what he looked like until his picture was posted on the TED site! He's got cool hair.
                      </li>
                     </ol>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>

                      TED Publishes My Video on TED-Ed!
                     </p>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Sunday, February 17, 2013
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="3999929314243972636">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/02/edible-science-model-projects-part-6.html">
                      Edible Science Model Projects, Part 6: 2nd Annual Periodic Table of Cupcakes
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3999929314243972636">
                     Our Second Annual Periodic Table of Cupcakes was a success!
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-oFUA9FAchac/USFC6n0qIQI/AAAAAAAALmg/shiBpTI4ho0/s1600/Periodic+Cupcake+2.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-oFUA9FAchac/USFC6n0qIQI/AAAAAAAALmg/shiBpTI4ho0/s320/Periodic+Cupcake+2.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-z3PbnszUVAI/USFC7HXz6AI/AAAAAAAALmk/QaYNPrG0vIA/s1600/Periodic+Cupcake+1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-z3PbnszUVAI/USFC7HXz6AI/AAAAAAAALmk/QaYNPrG0vIA/s320/Periodic+Cupcake+1.jpg" width="240"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GJWRCypE3iU/USFC7AOBPCI/AAAAAAAALmo/MAcBvT8XXWg/s1600/Periodic+Cupcake+3.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GJWRCypE3iU/USFC7AOBPCI/AAAAAAAALmo/MAcBvT8XXWg/s320/Periodic+Cupcake+3.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-txJ4DJa0xmI/USFC8LmkXEI/AAAAAAAALm4/PL6CPfRXAlg/s1600/Periodic+Cupcake+5.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="320" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-txJ4DJa0xmI/USFC8LmkXEI/AAAAAAAALm4/PL6CPfRXAlg/s320/Periodic+Cupcake+5.jpg" width="240"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-3mLWQjAhyK4/USFC8fyWKuI/AAAAAAAALm8/GpOWr5pnKC0/s1600/Periodic+Cupcake+4.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-3mLWQjAhyK4/USFC8fyWKuI/AAAAAAAALm8/GpOWr5pnKC0/s320/Periodic+Cupcake+4.jpg" width="240"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     If you want to do this sort of project these are things to keep in mind:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <ol>
                      <li>
                       Give students plenty of time to plan the project, shop for materials (parents don't like last minute requests) and to make the items that need to be made ahead of time (cupcakes/fondant icing). We have used a full period to plan it two weeks in advance. This gives you plenty of time to send a notice home, and plenty of time for parents and kids to shop and make things.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       This year, it took a little longer to build the table. I underestimated the difference in construction time that 4 fewer students would make--keep that in mind when you're doing this sort of project in your classroom. I use our 90 minute block period for table construction (with the cupcakes and fondant icing already made). Last year, with 11 students we finished it with time to take pictures and clean up. This year, with 8, it took two hours, PLUS clean up time. If you have a group of 20 students, with good planning you should be able to get it done in one class period.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       Make sure you have one copy of the periodic table per student. If you want the names of the "newest" elements, check online. Unununium has a new name now, and so do a few of the others!
                       <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=6&amp;cad=rja&amp;ved=0CF4QFjAF&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.llnl.gov%2Fnews%2Fnewsreleases%2F2012%2FMay%2FNR-12-05-07.html&amp;ei=K0AhUeT7G_Dx0wG97oGIAQ&amp;usg=AFQjCNFhcSICaGxYRBi3KLet0yNeV4_xmg&amp;sig2=fjH-ZAnSCHDmsFI0yBAvDw&amp;bvm=bv.42553238,d.dmg">
                        Mendelevium
                       </a>
                       ,
                       <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=6&amp;cad=rja&amp;ved=0CF4QFjAF&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.llnl.gov%2Fnews%2Fnewsreleases%2F2012%2FMay%2FNR-12-05-07.html&amp;ei=K0AhUeT7G_Dx0wG97oGIAQ&amp;usg=AFQjCNFhcSICaGxYRBi3KLet0yNeV4_xmg&amp;sig2=fjH-ZAnSCHDmsFI0yBAvDw&amp;bvm=bv.42553238,d.dmg">
                        Livermorium
                       </a>
                       and
                       <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=3&amp;cad=rja&amp;ved=0CEwQFjAC&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Feducation.jlab.org%2Fitselemental%2Fele112.html&amp;ei=G0AhUZyDBsjh0wHohoHwBA&amp;usg=AFQjCNGAFomlhkaKQLuY7uXO0fvkAptd-g&amp;sig2=GdOM5fJVXu9NMe5Ne4sbDQ&amp;bvm=bv.42553238,d.dmQ">
                        Copernicium
                       </a>
                       are a few.
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       I suggest doing this project towards the end of a unit on the periodic table. A great way to introduce the periodic table is by explaining why
                       <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=9&amp;cad=rja&amp;sqi=2&amp;ved=0CHkQFjAI&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aip.org%2Fhistory%2Fcurie%2Fperiodic.htm&amp;ei=HEEhUfaUM4q80AGe5IHIAQ&amp;usg=AFQjCNF60KC5ycbhrAQShHoT5Uw-TtEj1w&amp;sig2=Rbx0noCLrx-5uFV38ErNdg&amp;bvm=bv.42553238,d.dmg">
                        Dmitri Mendeleev
                       </a>
                       's creation was so extraordinary...use this TED-Ed Video to start it off right!
                      </li>
                     </ol>
                     <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="360" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/fPnwBITSmgU" width="580">
                     </iframe>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Edible Science Model Projects, Part 6: 2nd Annual Periodic Table of Cupcakes
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/02/edible-science-model-projects-part-6.html";
                     </script>

                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="5127436649291227845">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/01/ted-ed-invitation-lesson-of-my-life.html">
                      TED-Ed Invitation!  The Lesson of My Life!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5127436649291227845">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://assets.ed.tedcdn.com/assets/ted_ed_logo_header_beta-78fe9113cf87a37b613c5007678564fc.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="35" src="http://assets.ed.tedcdn.com/assets/ted_ed_logo_header_beta-78fe9113cf87a37b613c5007678564fc.png" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     I am amazed! I can't believe it! Someone nominated me to do a
                     <a href="http://ed.ted.com/">
                      TED-Ed
                     </a>
                     Lesson and my nomination was chosen!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I was nominated to do a lesson on the "Reasons for the Seasons". I am so excited that I can't even finish this post.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">

                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      TED-Ed Invitation!  The Lesson of My Life!
                     </p>

                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="7356805375677056607">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/01/this-is-amazing-my-7th-grade-students.html">
                      This is AMAZING!  My 7th grade students loved this TED talk...
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7356805375677056607">
                     I recommend showing this TED talk to all of your middle school students. Amy Cuddy discusses how to change your life by changing the position of your body for 2 minutes! My seventh graders absolutely loved this video: they had a quiz in French class right after their science class, so we spent the final three minutes of our class in a POWER POSE to lower cortisol levels and elevate testosterone!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://gradpost.ucsb.edu/storage/journal-image/powerpose.png?__SQUARESPACE_CACHEVERSION=1352508817025" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="184" src="http://gradpost.ucsb.edu/storage/journal-image/powerpose.png?__SQUARESPACE_CACHEVERSION=1352508817025" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Photo from Amy Cuddy's TED Talk showing an example of the POWER POSE that we used in class.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I also liked this video because it tells the story of how personal experience shaped Dr. Cuddy's research and the problem that she investigated. For those teachers who are focusing on teaching the scientific method, she clearly shows a slide that is her Problem Statement and discusses her hypothesis, as well as details on her experimental methods. She also displays graphs of her experimental measurements (hormone levels).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="360" mozallowfullscreen="" scrolling="no" src="http://embed.ted.com/talks/amy_cuddy_your_body_language_shapes_who_you_are.html" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="575">
                     </iframe>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      This is AMAZING!  My 7th grade students loved this TED talk...
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/01/this-is-amazing-my-7th-grade-students.html";
                     </script>
                     <script src="http://static.addtoany.com/menu/page.js" type="text/javascript">
                     </script>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Saturday, January 5, 2013
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="6034292287163448018">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/01/cell-cycle-game-for-middle-school-from.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Cell Cycle Game for Middle School from NobelPrize.org
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6034292287163448018">
                     This is a great game!
                     <br/>
                     <a href="http://www.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/2001/cellcycle.html">
                      http://www.nobelprize.org/educational/medicine/2001/cellcycle.html
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Requires Flash 5 browser plug-in.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     From the Nobel Prize site:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <h3 style="background-color: white; color: #024664; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 1.42em; font-weight: normal; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-top: 0px; padding-bottom: 10px;">
                      "Control of the Cell Cycle Game
                     </h3>
                     <div style="background-color: white; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.25em; margin-bottom: 15px;">
                      - What happens during ordinary cell division - mitosis?
                      <br/>
                      - What happens when a cell dies inside our body?
                      <br/>
                      - How does the body know when to make new cells?
                      <br/>
                      - What are the different phases in mitosis?
                      <br/>
                      - In what order does cell division occur and what ensures that nothing wrong happens?
                      <br/>
                      - How can a cancer tumor be formed?"
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Cell Cycle Game for Middle School from NobelPrize.org
                     </p>
