                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2013/01/quizlet-flash-card-set-for-mitosis.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Quizlet Flash Card Set for Mitosis
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5500165406045479335">
                     I love Quizlet! My students love Quizlet even more. I copied someone else's set on Quizlet, and made this new set--added a few images and Voila! Flashcards for you.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     My students especially like that you can print out flash cards or an alphabetized list...and the GAMES! Their favorite on the SMARTboard is the Scatter game. It's a fun way to study.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <iframe height="410" src="http://quizlet.com/18033761/familiarize/embedv2/?hideLinks" style="border: 0;" width="100%">
                     </iframe>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, November 20, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="5332773395802758726">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/11/i-feel-needthe-need-to-knead-baking-in.html">
                      I Feel the Need...the Need to Knead!  Baking in Science Class for Thanksgiving
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5332773395802758726">
                     A beautiful tradition at my small, independent Montessori school is of breaking bread with the entire school community (toddlers, middle-schoolers, teachers and staff) on the day before Thanksgiving.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     This year, in 7th year science class, we made a Hand-Kneaded Whole Wheat Bread, and had some science lessons along with it. I do this with the 7th years because they already had life science with me last year, and they understand anaerobic cellular respiration, proteins in living cells and cell division already.  I got the recipe from Cooks Illustrated (a science lab of cooking!) and the science to go along with it from various sources.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Here are the loaves prior to baking (student-made!):
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ToAmPmJ3dMM/UKvX4GzBviI/AAAAAAAAIzA/OGIil2znh_4/s1600/Bread+2012.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="300" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ToAmPmJ3dMM/UKvX4GzBviI/AAAAAAAAIzA/OGIil2znh_4/s400/Bread+2012.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Before Baking
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     Here's the recipe:
                     <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlWDUyYzdKQTE3X3c">
                      https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlWDUyYzdKQTE3X3c
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     Here's the science of browning techniques:
                     <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlZktOUlBBR2VKbUE">
                      https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlZktOUlBBR2VKbUE
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlTnlLa0tycjRyTVE">
                      Here's a chapter from the NSTA publication
                      <u>
                       Everyday Science Mysteries
                      </u>
                      on Baking Bread.
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-z7N1rnlRXwQ/UKvw86Jw-eI/AAAAAAAAI2Q/fYdCS1JeQTU/s1600/Bread+2+2012.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="300" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-z7N1rnlRXwQ/UKvw86Jw-eI/AAAAAAAAI2Q/fYdCS1JeQTU/s400/Bread+2+2012.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Hand-Kneaded Whole Wheat Bread after baking
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>

                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="6705360804525300162">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/11/edible-science-models-part-5-cell-cake.html">
                      Edible Science Model Projects: Part 5--Cell Cakes Project, Year #2
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6705360804525300162">
                     Last year, we did a Cell Cake Project in the grand tradition of edible science model-making! It was a tremendous success, and it remains
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/01/edible-science-model-projects-part-2.html">
                      the most popular post on my blog by far
                     </a>
                     !
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-8QD8pHsR3J8/ULY4gqdBjzI/AAAAAAAAJFg/EtsfusRCRsY/s144/2012-11-28_09-54-42_707.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="300" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-8QD8pHsR3J8/ULY4gqdBjzI/AAAAAAAAJFg/EtsfusRCRsY/s400/2012-11-28_09-54-42_707.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         This year's newest member of the project; The Bacterial Cell
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                     </div>
                     This year is the second year of the project, and I decided to make it meatier (or cakier, or whatever) by adding a research and presentation component to it, as well as adding critical thinking to the project by adding different cell types and asking students to compare and contrast them.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div style="background-color: white; color: #565555; font-family: Comfortaa, cursive; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px; text-align: center;">
                      <i>
                       "Remember, the primary goal of this project is to describe the similarities and differences between animal, plant and bacterial cells. "
                      </i>
                     </div>
                     <div style="background-color: white; color: #565555; font-family: Comfortaa, cursive; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px; text-align: center;">
                      <i>
                       -Mrs. Kaplan
                      </i>
                     </div>
                     <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: left; margin-right: 1em; text-align: left;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-XQPLmsRCVYI/ULY4gtPU1II/AAAAAAAAJFg/WcFmX2in3L4/s144/2012-11-28_09-54-05_820.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="300" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-XQPLmsRCVYI/ULY4gtPU1II/AAAAAAAAJFg/WcFmX2in3L4/s400/2012-11-28_09-54-05_820.jpg" width="400"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         This year's Plant Cell
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <ul>
                      <li>
                       <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlTkh6Tzctem5xbms">
                        A descriptive list of the required elements of the Cell Cake Project
                       </a>
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       <a href="http://allrecipes.com/recipe/marshmallow-fondant/">
                        The super-easy and yummy Marshmallow Fondant recipe that kids can use for labeling and other structures.
                       </a>
                      </li>
                      <li>
                       <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlSVFueUZVQnNfdms">
                        Venn diagram organizer for plant, bacterial and animal cells
                       </a>
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                     <div>
                      <div style="background-color: white; color: #565555; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px;">
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                         <br/>
                        </span>
                       </b>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">

                       </b>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                         <br/>

                       </b>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">

                         <br/>

                       </b>
                       <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                        <tbody>
                         <tr>
                          <td style="text-align: center;">
                           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-DBtjGehvizM/ULY4gmgW-DI/AAAAAAAAJFg/VgEMasBOfXs/s144/2012-11-28_09-54-58_861.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                            <img border="0" height="300" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-DBtjGehvizM/ULY4gmgW-DI/AAAAAAAAJFg/VgEMasBOfXs/s400/2012-11-28_09-54-58_861.jpg" width="400"/>
                           </a>
                          </td>
                         </tr>
                         <tr>
                          <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                           The Animal Cell--this cake was saved from a crumbly death by a large batch of delicious homemade fondant icing.
                          </td>
                         </tr>
                        </tbody>
                       </table>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                        </span>
                       </b>
                       <br/>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                        </span>
                       </b>
                       <b>
                        <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                         Cell Anatomy Resources:
                        </span>
                       </b>
                      </div>
                      <div style="background-color: white; color: #565555; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px;">
                       <ul>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <b>
                          <u>
                           <i>
                            <span style="color: #990000; font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                             RESEARCH FORM:
                             <a href="http://www.iecc.edu/wvc/lrc/resrws.pdf" rel="nofollow" style="color: #1c878a;">
                              http://www.iecc.edu/wvc/lrc/resrws.pdf
                             </a>
                            </span>
                           </i>
                          </u>
                         </b>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          <a href="http://www.johnkyrk.com/CellIndex.html" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://www.johnkyrk.com/CellIndex.html
                          </a>
                          --this site has several links in the drop-down menu that could be useful in identifying additional structures or more detailed explanations that would be helpful in making your poster/model. For example
                          <a href="http://www.johnkyrk.com/golgiAlone.html" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://www.johnkyrk.com/golgiAlone.html
                          </a>
                          has detailed descriptions of how the Golgi body works.
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          <a href="http://www.cellsalive.com/cells/3dcell.htm" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://www.cellsalive.com/cells/3dcell.htm
                          </a>
                          has interactive models of all three cell types.
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          Interactive diagram of a bacterial cell:
                          <a href="http://www.neok12.com/diagram/Microorganisms-01.htm" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://www.neok12.com/diagram/Microorganisms-01.htm
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          Bacterial cell:
                          <a href="http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/bacteriacell.html" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/bacteriacell.html
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                       </ul>
                       <ul>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          Animal cell:
                          <a href="http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/animalcell.html" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/animalcell.html
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          Plant cell:
                          <a href="http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/plantcell.html" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://micro.magnet.fsu.edu/cells/plantcell.html
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          Inside the Cell PDF booklet (full color illustrations):
                          <a href="http://publications.nigms.nih.gov/insidethecell/pdf/inside_the_cell.pdf" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://publications.nigms.nih.gov/insidethecell/pdf/inside_the_cell.pdf
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          **Wikipedia:
                          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_(biology)" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_(biology)
                          </a>
                          --this site can be used as a STARTING PLACE to find information. Keep in mind, that Wikipedia has gathered it's information from other places...those places are listed (with links) at the bottom of the page.
                          <b>
                           <i>
                            Those
                           </i>
                          </b>
                          are the links that should be used in your research forms, NOT "en.wikipedia.org".
                         </span>
                        </li>
                       </ul>
                      </div>
                      <div style="background-color: white; color: #565555; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px;">
                       <ul>
                        <li style="list-style-position: outside; list-style-type: circle;">
                         <span style="color: black; font-family: Times, Times New Roman, serif;">
                          <a href="http://cellimagelibrary.org/" rel="nofollow" style="color: #89a9aa;">
                           http://cellimagelibrary.org/
                          </a>
                         </span>
                        </li>
                       </ul>
                      </div>
                     </div>

                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="2043767845894098381">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/quizlet-flashcard-set-on-moon-phases.html">
                      Teaching Tools Series: Quizlet Flashcard Set on Moon Phases, Eclipses and Tides
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2043767845894098381">
                     I have a new role model and her name is
                     <a href="http://quizlet.com/blog/meet-joan-le-science-teacher/">
                      Joan Le
                     </a>
                     , author of science-teaching blog extraordinaire,
                     <a href="http://www.thescienceroom.org/">
                      The Science Room
                     </a>
                     . I haven't met her in person, and I don't need to in order to appreciate her innovative integration of technology into her classroom. This flashcard set on
                     <a href="http://quizlet.com/features/">
                      Quizlet
                     </a>
                     is a gift from her, that I am posting so more people can find it.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <iframe height="410" src="http://quizlet.com/15550282/familiarize/embedv2/?hideLinks" style="border: 0;" width="100%">
                     </iframe>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>

                      Teaching Tools Series: Quizlet Flashcard Set on Moon Phases, Eclipses and Tides
                     </p>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Friday, October 19, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="6512912036422958446">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/difficult-concepts-teaching-reason-for.html">
                      Difficult Concepts: Teaching the Reason for the Seasons in Middle School
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6512912036422958446">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <iframe allowfullscreen="" class="YOUTUBE-iframe-video" data-thumbnail-src="https://ytimg.googleusercontent.com/vi/DD_8Jm5pTLk/0.jpg" frameborder="0" height="266" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/DD_8Jm5pTLk?feature=player_embedded" width="320">
                      </iframe>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     My
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2011/12/exploring-reason-for-seasons-in-middle.html#.UIFvf2_R74Y">
                      last post on teaching the reason for the seasons in middle school
                     </a>
                     focused on the biggest misconception of most people when it comes to the concept, and an excellent curricular resource that I have successfully used for years to help teach this concept that is difficult to teach. It is difficult to teach mainly because of the misconceptions that many people (including very smart people--some of them are teachers!).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I didn't even talk about the ACTUAL reasons--I spent all of my time on UNTEACHING a misconception, which is one of the challenges of being a science teacher! Kids come to us with all sorts of ideas about how the world works, and we have to ensure experiences that help them understand what is right about their models and what ideas need, ahem, "reworking". So here they are:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Here is a summary of the reasons for the seasons:
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.physicalgeography.net/fundamentals/images/seasons.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="284" src="http://www.physicalgeography.net/fundamentals/images/seasons.jpg" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.physicalgeography.net/fundamentals/6h.html" style="background-color: white; color: #6699cc; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; line-height: 25px; text-align: start; text-decoration: none; word-spacing: 1px;">
                          <span style="font-size: xx-small;">
                           Images fromhttp://www.physicalgeography.net/fundamentals/6h.html
                          </span>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     1. The big, overarching, reason for the seasons is that the Earth is tilted 23.5 degrees from vertical on its rotational axis; and the Earth revolves around the Sun with the axis always pointing in the same "direction" in space. This results in several phenomena:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <ul>
                      <li>
                       The number of daylight hours a region receives varies based on latitude and season. If the Earth were not tilted, it would be like an equinox every day: 12 hours of sunlight and 12 hours of darkness. In the northern hemisphere, in summer, Connecticut gets around 15 hours of daylight each day and 9 hours of darkness. As you move north in latitude, the number of daylight hours in summer
                       <i>
                        increases
                       </i>
                       , so Anchorage, Alaska would get 19 hours of daylight on the same day that Jacksonville, Florida gets 14.
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-day-length-2.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="192" src="http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-day-length-2.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-day-length-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="224" src="http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-day-length-1.jpg" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-photoperiod.html">
                          http://www.paulnoll.com/Oregon/Birds/climate-photoperiod.html
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <ul>
                      <li>
                       When there is daylight on a part of the Earth it warms up. When there is darkness, it cools off. In the summer, New England warms up for 15 hours or so and then cools off for 9 hours. It warms for longer than it cools...this happens day after day after day so there is an overall warming effect.  In the winter, the opposite happens: there are many more hours of cooling time--15 hours of darkness--than warming time (9 hours) and day after day, this results in a cooling effect.
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                     <div>
                      2. The other reason for the seasons is that the Earth is a sphere and so the solar intensity per unit of surface area differs based on latitude and time of year.
                      <i>
                      </i>
                      <b style="font-style: italic;">
                       If daylight hours were the only thing that determined the average temperature at a certain latitude, then areas above the Arctic Circle would be the hottest places on Earth in Northern Summer, because it receives 24 hours of daylight (see chart above).
                      </b>
                      So, there has to be some other factor at work here: many equatorial regions only have two seasons--hot and wet or hot and dry! It's always hotter there than at the poles. The solution is solar intensity per unit of area which changes based on the angular height of the sun.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <ul>
                       <li>
                        Angular height of the Sun in the sky changes throughout the day, with the Sun at it's highest point at solar noon; it also changes throughout the year, as shown in these diagrams:
                       </li>
                      </ul>
                     </div>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.extension.org/sites/default/files/styles/large/public/Solar_Air_Solar_Exposure.gif" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="172" src="http://www.extension.org/sites/default/files/styles/large/public/Solar_Air_Solar_Exposure.gif" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         Angular height of the Sun at 40 degrees Northern Latitude at different times of the year.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.extension.org/sites/default/files/styles/large/public/SunAltitude.gif" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="257" src="http://www.extension.org/sites/default/files/styles/large/public/SunAltitude.gif" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://www.extension.org/pages/62239/identify-sun-and-shade-areas-in-the-landscape">
                          http://www.extension.org/pages/62239/identify-sun-and-shade-areas-in-the-landscape
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <div>
                      <ul>
                       <li>
                        Solar intensity changes in proportion with angular height.A great activity to do with students is using a flashlight held at constant height over a piece of graph paper. Trace the outline of the circle of light and then tilt the flashlight slightly. The new shape is an oval with a much larger surface area (count and compare the squares) over which the same amount of light is spread. So the solar intensity per unit of area in the image to the right is much less.
                       </li>
                      </ul>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://frank.mtsu.edu/~cdharris/GEOL100/weather/Fig1b.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                        <img border="0" height="160" src="http://frank.mtsu.edu/~cdharris/GEOL100/weather/Fig1b.jpg" width="400"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                       Now my post is too long, and I have to teach a class in 5 minutes!
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>

                      Difficult Concepts: Teaching the Reason for the Seasons in Middle School
                     </p>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Thursday, October 18, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="678202633431442776">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/boy-oh-boy-cellular-biology-and.html">
                      Boy oh, boy!  Cellular biology and immunology have come a long way since I was in college!
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-678202633431442776">
                     The last time I took a college course in cellular biology or immunology it was about 1994. Since I am a science teacher, my professional journal-reading tends to concentrate on methodologyresearch in science education, for example:
                     <a href="http://www.nsta.org/middleschool/">
                      Science Scope
                     </a>
                     ,
                     <a href="http://www.tcrecord.org/">
                      Teachers College Record
                     </a>
                     , or the
                     <a href="http://www.springer.com/education+%26+language/science+education/journal/10956">
                      Journal of Science Education and Technology
                     </a>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     <i>
                      <br/>
                     </i>
                     Because of that, I live for "current events" projects or assignments in my classes. It gives me and my students an opportunity to dive into what fascinates us about science at the cutting edge. One of my tools for current events is my TED-talk-Tuesdays! I choose a few TED talks from
                     <a href="http://ted.com/">
                      TED.com
                     </a>
                     and show them to my classes after previewing them (always preview your TED talks! you want to be prepared for jokes by the presenter or images--diagrams of human anatomy and such--that the kids may not be expecting).
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     My mind was blown today, though! The talk we watched today was by David Bolinsky, medical director of
                     <a href="http://multimedia.mcb.harvard.edu/">
                      BioVisions biological animations studio at Harvard University
                     </a>
                     . It is amazing to me how much MORE we know now about the molecular mechanisms inside the cell than we did when I was in college! I feel like I need to go back to school just to catch up!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     After watching the talk, I searched around the internet for the full version of the amazing 3-dimensional animated, narrated and annotated video and found it here:
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div id="neovid" style="width: 485px;">
                      <b>
                       The Inner Life of a Cell - Harvard University
                      </b>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="margin: 7px 0px 7px 0px;">
                       <object classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" height="385" id="neoply333" width="480">
                        <param name="movie" value="http://www.neok12.com/plyem.swf?yi=yX65036d526d5e7b0e580f46">
                        </param>
                        <param name="quality" value="high">
                        </param>
                        <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
                        </param>
                        <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
                        </param>
                        <param name="loop" value="false">
                        </param>
                        <param name="menu" value="false">
                        </param>
                        <embed allowfullscreen="true" allowscriptaccess="always" height="385" loop="false" menu="false" quality="high" src="http://www.neok12.com/plyem.swf?yi=yX65036d526d5e7b0e580f46" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
                        </embed>
                       </object>
                      </div>
                      <div style="font-size: 12px; text-align: right;">
                       More
                       <a href="http://www.neok12.com/">
                        science games
                       </a>
                       &amp; videos on
                       <a href="http://www.neok12.com/Cell-Structures.htm">
                        Cell Structures
                       </a>
                       at NeoK12.com
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     I found it helpful to also view the same process in an animation format that was less visually complicated. For a traditional flash animation of the same process (shown in 2D) with labels and explanations, click this link:
                     <a href="http://multimedia.mcb.harvard.edu/flash/extravasation.swf">
                      http://multimedia.mcb.harvard.edu/flash/extravasation.swf
                     </a>
                     <br/>

                      Boy oh, boy!  Cellular biology and immunology have come a long way since I was in college!

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, October 9, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="2819731352167337585">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/i-absolutely-love-my-job-aka-best.html">
                      I absolutely love my job!  (aka Best Science Teacher Annual Goal...Ever!)
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2819731352167337585">
                     <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-OCsJ9fHv8ag/TyyxVSU1BkI/AAAAAAAADOQ/A3Oo2EnX7CA/s1600/periodic+4.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                      <img border="0" height="320" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-OCsJ9fHv8ag/TyyxVSU1BkI/AAAAAAAADOQ/A3Oo2EnX7CA/s320/periodic+4.jpg" width="213"/>
                     </a>
                     Like many professions, each year teachers create professional goals that they would like to accomplish for the year. Establishing these goals is meant to spur the development of a set of professional skills. Periodically throughout the year, teachers meet with supervisors to discuss progress on the goals and to collaboratively problem-solve any items that are hindering accomplishing of the goals.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Last year at my final 'goal progress' meeting, I met with other teachers to discuss our goals and talk about ideas for goals for the present school year. I had the BEST idea for a goal...it was the kind of idea that makes you so excited to get started on accomplishing it! What a way to love your job.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Here is what I wrote:
                     <br/>
                     <div class="MsoNormal">
                      <i>
                       "Goal : To develop a thematic tradition in the middle
school science classroom of Celebrating Science and to begin bringing that
theme outward into the community.
                      </i>
                     </div>
                     <div class="MsoNormal">
                      <i>
                       <b>
                        Steps I will take to achieve that goal:
                       </b>
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </i>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/--JWqQeyYHZ4/TyLimyX-Q6I/AAAAAAAADEw/zjCoHN2ccdI/s320/Cell+Cake+Nucleus+closeup.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/--JWqQeyYHZ4/TyLimyX-Q6I/AAAAAAAADEw/zjCoHN2ccdI/s320/Cell+Cake+Nucleus+closeup.JPG"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <ul style="margin-top: 0in;" type="disc">
                      <li class="MsoNormal">
                       <i>
                        To develop lessons,
     materials or events in science class that
                        <b>
                         celebrate science
                        </b>
                        . For example: to create special thematic
     lab experiments and classroom decorations for Halloween; to organize
     events that
                        <b>
                         celebrate the astronomical phenomena
                        </b>
                        of the changing of the
     seasons, lunar or solar eclipses, milestones in sciencelike Newtons
     birthday, or to further develop events like last years
                        <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/02/periodic-table-of-cupcakes.html#.UHRiYi7R74Y">
                         Periodic Table of     the Cupcakes
                        </a>
                        or the
                        <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/01/edible-science-model-projects-part-2.html#.UHRiaS7R74Y">
                         Cell Cake Project.
                        </a>
                       </i>
                      </li>
                      <li class="MsoNormal">
                       <i>
                        <b>
                         To build community
     awareness and anticipation of the events
                        </b>
                        with the school newsletters, parent
     awareness email blasts and other media.
                        <o:p>
                        </o:p>
                       </i>
                      </li>
                      <li class="MsoNormal">
                       <i>
                        To guide middle school
     students to create ways of
                        <b>
                         sharing the actual happening of the event with
     younger students in the school.
                        </b>
                        For
     example, by visiting the classes and sharing the Periodic Table Cupcakes
     with them after explaining what the project was all about and answering
     questions from the younger students."
                       </i>
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                     <div>
                      <b>
                       This entire goal can translate from teacher-ese into English as: "Spend your energy on
                       <i>
                        how to have fun
                       </i>
                       in science class!"
                      </b>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <b>
                       <br/>
                      </b>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      So this year, as I plan Halloween Science in the lab (Halloween falls on our extended-period lab day this year--Hooray!) I can have fun planning it...get really 'into it' and elaborate on it, develop it into something that excites even me! All the while, I know I am working on accomplishing a professional goal that I set for myself which adds to my feeling of satisfaction about it.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      I will definitely post about my Halloween Science Day this year and other events...but not yet...some of my students and parents read this blog and I don't want to give anything away. If you need some ideas,
                      <a href="http://www.sciencebob.com/blog/?p=360">
                       try this link to Science Bob's
                      </a>
                      site of Halloween science demos.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      By the way, a big shout-out to Liisa Petersen, who is one of the best science teachers I have EVER met, and an absolute pro at loving her job and having fun.
                      <a href="http://teacherweb.com/Blog/CT/MiddlesexMiddleSchool/Flugtag/1/default.aspx">
                       One thing that is on the list this year is to try to model her FLUGTAG event.
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      I absolutely love my job!  (aka Best Science Teacher Annual Goal...Ever!)
                     </p>

                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Saturday, October 6, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="5528577078346926009">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://mariamontessori.com/mm/?p=2136#.UHDXjfutcDE.blogger">
                      If At First You Dont Succeed GREAT!!  Maria Montessori
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5528577078346926009">
                     <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      This article explains why a Montessori Education can be the key to an extraordinary beginning in the sciences, or any investigative field:
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <a href="http://mariamontessori.com/mm/?p=2136#.UHDXjfutcDE.blogger">
                      <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                       If At First You Dont Succeed GREAT!!  Maria Montessori
                      </span>
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <br/>
                     </span>
                     <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                      <span style="background-color: white; color: #333333; line-height: 18px;">
                       This is one of the most important things about a good science program, too! My students were laughing the other day after watching an amusing TED talk by a researcher who said, "Do you know how I know that I made a measurement error? Beca
                      </span>
                     </span>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="text_exposed_show" style="background-color: white; color: #333333; display: inline; line-height: 18px;">
                      <span style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
                       use that (dot on the graph/outlier) is messing up my data!" Guiding students to become friendly with error is essential in science because that is where many of the great discoveries have come from: what is assumed to be error or anomaly is actually a great discovery. Case in point: Kepler's ellipses.
                      </span>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      If At First You Dont Succeed GREAT!!  Maria Montessori
                     </p>
                     <script type="text/javascript">
                      var a2a_config = a2a_config || {};a2a_config.linkname_escape=1;a2a_config.linkurl="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/if-at-first-you-dont-succeed-great.html";
                     </script>
                     <script src="http://static.addtoany.com/menu/page.js" type="text/javascript">
                     </script>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Tuesday, October 2, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="7348442717172609988">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/10/ted-talk-tuesdays-science-of-happiness.html">
                      TED Talk Tuesdays: The Science Of Happiness and Living Extraordinary Lives
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7348442717172609988">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oPwiciiU0EY/UGsQ6oJtpSI/AAAAAAAAH5k/OlNhmitB5Wc/s1600/flourish.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="200" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oPwiciiU0EY/UGsQ6oJtpSI/AAAAAAAAH5k/OlNhmitB5Wc/s200/flourish.jpg" width="129"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     Last year a friend gave me
                     <a href="http://www.biblio.com/books/534145246.html">
                      a book called
                      <span style="color: purple;">
                       <u>
                        Flourish
                       </u>
                      </span>
                     </a>
                     by Martin E. P. Seligman, a professor of psychology at the
                     <a href="http://www.ppc.sas.upenn.edu/">
                      University of Pennsylvania.
                     </a>
                     I didn't read it. Until this summer. I highly recommend this book to educators, business people, members of the military or people who love someone.
                     <a href="http://www.thehappinessinstitute.com/blog/article.aspx?c=3&amp;a=2909">
                      Click here for an extremely biased review of the book.
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     As a scientist, the ideas in this book appeal to me because the findings about improving well-being and happiness and the techniques that
                     <a href="http://www.ppc.sas.upenn.edu/bio.htm">
                      Dr. Seligman
                     </a>
                     presents and teaches in his book are research-based. Life is short. If I don't have to figure stuff out by trial-and-error, if I can just try something new that is proven to work--
                     <b>
                      great!
                     </b>
                     I'm a working mother of two. It saves me time and improves my satisfaction with my life. I definitely have had a few, "if I only knew this when I was younger.." moments while reading this book.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     As a teacher of adolescents, this book and the
                     <a href="http://www.ppc.sas.upenn.edu/positiveeducation.htm">
                      UPenn Positive Psychology Center website
                     </a>
                     gives me concrete, ready-to-use tools
                     <a href="http://www.ppc.sas.upenn.edu/teachinghighschool.htm">
                      (like this complete 7-day curriculum on teaching positive psychology to adolescents)
                     </a>
                     that I can use with my students to help them learn to take an active role in improving their relationships with each other, their satisfaction with school and life and improving their outlook on life in a cognitively lasting way.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Today was TED Talk Tuesdays in my classroom. We watch TED talks for science and technology current events and to observe effective presentation styles. Here is the talk we watched today.
                     <a href="http://www.ted.com/speakers/shawn_achor.html">
                      Shawn Achor
                     </a>
                     is a psychology researcher and professor at Harvard University and
                     <a href="http://goodthinkinc.com/">
                      CEO of GoodThink, Inc
                     </a>
                     . His positive psychology class at Harvard in 2006 was
                     <a href="http://www.thecrimson.com/article/2006/2/15/the-science-of-smiling-strongcorrection-appendedstrongbrbr845/">
                      the most popular psychology class in Harvard's history
                     </a>
                     . He also happens to be a very effective--and funny--presenter. He presents many of the ideas that Seligman discusses in his book. Watch out! He only has 12 minutes and he talks really fast! Enjoy!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>

                  <span>
                   Monday, August 13, 2012
                  </span>

                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="4311293733059058408">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/08/the-science-of-getting-kids-to-eat.html">
                      The Science of Getting Kids to Eat Their Veggies
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4311293733059058408">
                     This is more of a culinary post from another blog that I contribute to called
                     <a href="http://btchnktchn.blogspot.com/">
                      Bitchin' in the Kitchen
                     </a>
                     , but I liked the results so much (of the public response to the post AND the actual food produced by following the recipe!) that I wanted to post it here.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://encrypted-tbn0.google.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcR0RG1MuKoXzxx96thxsSrupzkPMsaHfPxuY5oCQ6FCyDHRKAzy" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" src="https://encrypted-tbn0.google.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcR0RG1MuKoXzxx96thxsSrupzkPMsaHfPxuY5oCQ6FCyDHRKAzy"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     I am totally not kidding! Dairy free and full of green veggies.
                     <br/>
                     This is a crazy recipe, but it tastes amazing! More important for me, there's no dairy-hangover.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>

                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Thursday, August 2, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="8964020602295447179">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/08/miscellaneous-astronomy-awesomeness.html">
                      Teaching Tools: Astronomy Awesomeness:  NASA eclipses, Moon "wobble" video, Scale of the Universe interactive
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8964020602295447179">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://eclipse.gsfc.nasa.gov/image/bannerEclipse2008.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="57" src="http://eclipse.gsfc.nasa.gov/image/bannerEclipse2008.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     The NASA eclipse site: with thorough charts and lists of future and past lunar and solar eclipses. Exhaustive resource.
                     <a href="http://eclipse.gsfc.nasa.gov/eclipse.html">
                      http://eclipse.gsfc.nasa.gov/eclipse.html
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="https://encrypted-tbn2.google.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcSQ1e3NIv--DFb2evckrWsEwIvnkMxVBcYeRz93u2FPU9rP6Qt1" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" src="https://encrypted-tbn2.google.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcSQ1e3NIv--DFb2evckrWsEwIvnkMxVBcYeRz93u2FPU9rP6Qt1"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     Scale of the Universe interactive (Fantastic on a SMART board!) by the Huang twins (high school students!).
                     <a href="http://htwins.net/scale2/">
                      http://htwins.net/scale2/
                     </a>
                     beautiful graphics and music.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>

                      Teaching Tools: Astronomy Awesomeness:  NASA eclipses, Moon "wobble" video, Scale of the Universe interactive
                     </p>

                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/08/yale-peabody-fellows-institute-sun-and.html">
                      Yale Peabody Fellows Institute, The Sun and Resources Continued
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6888952839785281643">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      <b>
                       <u>
                        Resources
                       </u>
                      </b>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      <b>
                       <u>
                        <a href="https://docs.google.com/open?id=0B2mVNulXvlPlZmtMaXB1aDdEMXM">
                         Motherlode: Click here for a FULL FOLDER of resources on the Sun (including beautiful powerpoint lessons, movies and a complete, 108 page curriculum from the Solar Dynamics Observatory (NASA)
                        </a>
                       </u>
                      </b>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      <b>
                       <u>
                        <br/>
                       </u>
                      </b>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;">
                      Below, I have links to sites and a lesson plan on charting sunspots with real SOHO data.
                     </div>

                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, August 1, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="1880283460654065881">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://scienceandtechnologylady.blogspot.com/2012/08/yale-peabody-astronomy-day-2-sunspots.html">
                      Yale-Peabody Astronomy--Day 2, Part 1: Sunspots
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1880283460654065881">
                     My head is spinning! We learned so much today...lectures on gravity, the Sun, meteorites and meteors! Okay, one topic at a time: Sunspots.
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FZOkbIbXw9g/UBmYaBOC4nI/AAAAAAAAGik/aIVJsWhlEnE/s1600/sunspotter.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FZOkbIbXw9g/UBmYaBOC4nI/AAAAAAAAGik/aIVJsWhlEnE/s320/sunspotter.jpg" width="320"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         This is the sunspotter tool that we used today.
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <u>
                      <br/>
                     </u>
                     <br/>
                     Today, we got a chance to practice using a Sunspotter telescope. An ingenious tool to safely view sunspots on the surface of the sun. The Peabody Museum has purchased a supply of these tools and as part of the Fellowship, we can borrow them for about 1 month to do sunspot investigations with our students.
                     <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Carolina-Biological-Supply-Company-Sunspotter/dp/B0062BEOVC">
                      You can purchase one here.
                     </a>
                     Charting sunspot locations over a period of time can be used to show that the Sun rotates, and can be used to discover the direction of rotation of the Sun. One interesting thing that I noticed, was that the Sun moved out of the field of view
                     <i>
                      unbelievably quickly!
                     </i>
                     Every couple of minutes, the Earth would rotate enough so that the image of the Sun was completely off of the viewing platform.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I was quite surprised by this, and
                     <a href="http://www.astro.yale.edu/people/michael-faison">
                      Dr. Michael Faison
                     </a>
                     , astronomy professor and Director of the Leitner Observatory and Planetarium at Yale confirmed that the Sun's apparent motion is one solar diameter approximately every 2 minutes! Fascinating!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Right here, you can see today's image of the Sun from
                     <a href="http://spaceweather.com/">
                      Spaceweather.com
                     </a>
                     . In the image, you can see many sunspots. When we were using the Sunspotter, we could see 4 of the largest of them.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;">
                      <tbody>
                       <tr>
                        <td style="text-align: center;">
                         <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-p2WJQkCMFKM/UBmath0lmlI/AAAAAAAAGis/QnvhXVu5wTo/s1600/sun1aug12.gif" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                          <img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-p2WJQkCMFKM/UBmath0lmlI/AAAAAAAAGis/QnvhXVu5wTo/s1600/sun1aug12.gif"/>
                         </a>
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                       <tr>
                        <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                         A visible light image of the sunspots from Spaceweather.com
                        </td>
                       </tr>
                      </tbody>
                     </table>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <a class="a2a_dd" href="http://www.addtoany.com/share_save">
                      <img alt="Share/Bookmark" border="0" height="16" src="http://static.addtoany.com/buttons/share_save_171_16.png" width="171"/>
                     </a>
                     <p class="a2a_linkname_escape" style="display:none">
                      Yale-Peabody Astronomy--Day 2, Part 1: Sunspots
                     </p>

                <h2>
                 About Me
                </h2>
                <div class="widget-content">
                 <a href="https://plus.google.com/104182891877689694057">
                  <img alt="My photo" class="profile-img" height="80" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/-ASyFsbKHsWk/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAYyM/3VGNuxb8OiY/s80-c/photo.jpg" width="80"/>
                 </a>
                 <dl class="profile-datablock">
                  <dt class="profile-data">
                   <a class="profile-name-link g-profile" href="https://plus.google.com/104182891877689694057" rel="author" style="background-image: url(//www.google.com/images/icons/ui/gprofile_button-16.png);">
                    Rebecca Kaplan
                   </a>

                  </dt>
                  <dd class="profile-data">
                  </dd>
                  <dd class="profile-textblock">
                   I'm a mom, science teacher and blogger (in that order). Although I've been teaching for a lot longer than I've been a mom (18 years teaching), those little ones kind of take over once they get here, don't they--to my great joy! I think being a mom has helped me to be a better teacher and it DEFINITELY helped me to become a better blogger--STL is my second blog--the first one was one to share pictures of the kids with my family and friends.
                  </dd>
